Berlin 41-25H Well Evaluation
INTRODUCTION
The Berlin 41-25H well [NE NE Section 25, T151N, R93W] is located approximately ~8 miles
southwest of New Town in Mountrail County, North Dakota. The Berlin 41-25H is a Middle
Bakken Member, horizontal well within the Williston Basin consisting of a single ~10,000' long
lateral drilled towards the south at a proposed direction of 177.09°. The vertical hole was drilled
to 9,872' MD in the Lodgepole Formation, and the curve was landed at a depth of 10,656' MD in
the Middle Bakken Member. Directional drilling and geo-steering techniques were then used to
maintain maximum exposure to the target zone.
OFFSET CONTROL
Multiple offset wells were available within Reunion Bay Field, but control was limited to three
wells in close proximity (Figure 1). These three wells include:
The Marathon Oil Co., Brodahl 31-25H [NW NE Section 25, T151N, R93W]
which is located 2' south and 195' west of the subject well.
The Marathon Oil Co., Moritz USA 11-30H [NE NE Section 25, T151N,
R93W] which is located 66' east of subject well.
The Marathon Oil Co., Zook 41-25TFH [NE NE Section 25, T151N, R93W]
which is located 33' east of the subject well.
Real time gamma signatures were constantly compared to the previously mentioned offset wells
to ensure accuracy of the landing depth. The prognosis called for a landing target of 10,322'
TVD. Most tops, below the Lodgepole Formation top, came in around 4' low and the target was
dropped 4' upon picking the L3000 marker. The curve eventually landed at 10,324' TVD, 2'
high to the intended landing target but within the upper half of the defined target zone.
OPERATIONS
Pats Consulting & Solsten XP provided well-site supervision. Baker Hughes Inteq provided
directional drilling and MWD services during. Sunburst Consulting, Inc. provided well-site
geology consulting. Drilling fluids were provided for and analyzed daily by Mi Swaco.
The well was spud on October 21, 2014 by H&P rig #256. A 12 1/4" hole was drilled using
freshwater, with one tri-cone bit to 2,055' MD, at which point a 9 " casing string was set and
cemented to surface. After casing, a diesel invert mud system was used with mud weights
ranging from 9.8-10.1 pounds/gallon and associated viscosities ranging from 49-62
seconds/quart. The vertical hole was drilled to a kick-off point (KOP) of 9,872' MD, in just over
80.6 drilling hours, with three 8 ¾" PDC bits over three bottom-hole assembly (BHA) runs.
The curve started on October 27, 2014. One 8 ¾" PDC bit, in front of a 2.12° fixed motor,
drilled the curve to 10,656' MD, 10,324' TVD in 13.3 hours. A 7" casing string was then set and
cemented to 10,641' MD within the Middle Bakken Member.
The lateral portion of the well began on October 30, 2014, switching over to the salt water mud
system with mud weights ranging from 5.7 ­ 10.2 pound/gallon and viscosities ranging between
10.2-30 seconds/quart. The lateral assemblies included two 6" PDC bits, 1.4°, 1.5° fixed mud
motors, agitators and MWD tools. The entire lateral was drilled with two bottom hole
assemblies, drilling the lateral in 51.4 hours and the entire well in 147.68 hours. The only trip
occurred at 17,692' MD, due to a failed MWD tool. The Berlin 41-25H reached a total depth
(TD) of 20,500' MD on November 4, 2014, after 14.5 drilling days. The bottom-hole location is
estimated to be 10,053.39' south & 516.72' east of surface location or approximately 228.75' FSL
& 628.28' FEL, SE SE Section 36, T151N, R93W (Figure 1).

GEOLOGY
Lithology
Lithology descriptions and sample analysis
began in the Kibbey Formation and were
continuously monitored through the Charles,
Mission Canyon, and Lodgepole formations
before penetrating the targeted Bakken
Formation.
The Middle Bakken Member was logged at
10,307' TVD (-8,355' MSL). It consists of
siltstone, limestone and silty sandstone. The
targeted, silty sandstone section contained
fair intergranular porosity and trace to rare
amounts of spotty, light brown oil staining
(Figure 2).
Figure 2. Photograph of M. Bakken, silty sandstone.
Geo-steering
The ideal target zone was defined as a 10' interval, the top of which was set 14' below the base
of the Upper Bakken Shale Member. Low gamma markers (approx. 40-50 API) located above
the top and below the base of target, moderate gamma markers (approx. 70-80 API) within
target, and high gamma markers (~90 API) below the target zone proved to be the most useful
signatures for geo-steering (Figure 3).
Figure 3. TVD gamma signatures from the Berlin 41-25H curve landing (left) and a close offset well (MOC, 2014).
Offset wells indicated that the formation lies approximately flat for the first 2,000' of vertical
section, then downwards at ~0.2°, from 16,000' to 17,000', before gradually rising to ~0.1° until
total depth. The final gross apparent dip, from landing to the end of the lateral, was estimated at
-0.08° (Figure 4). Geo-steering techniques exposed 95% of uncased borehole to the Middle
Bakken ideal target.

Hydrocarbons
Background gas remained near 200 units until total depth with three exceptions: from 12,500'-
14,862' MD and 18,075'- 19,512' MD background was near 350 units, and from 19,512' MD to
total depth background registered ~450 units. Higher gas sections exhibited multiple total gas
peaks greater than 500+ units. The highest gas value recorded was a trip gas of 1,246 units at
10,656 MD (Figure 4).
Drill fluid was vented to the gas buster from 10,656' to 14,768' MD, flowed through the gas
buster from 14,768' to 18,075' MD, then was vented until total depth. The entire target zone
was observed to contain relatively moderate gas concentrations and consistent oil staining.

SUMMARY
The Marathon Oil Company Berlin 41-25H was spud on October 21, 2014 and reached total
depth on November 4, 2014, after 14.5 drilling days. Samples from the Middle Bakken target
presented as a gray to brown silty sandstone, containing trace light brown spotty oil stain and
fair intergranular porosity. MWD gamma-ray markers, sample analysis, and penetration rates
were successfully utilized to expose 95% of the lateral borehole to the ideal Middle Bakken
target. Total gas values were moderate throughout the entire lateral with a higher sections
derived from: 12,500'-14,862' MD, 18,075'- 19,512' MD, and 19,512' MD to total depth.
Consistent oil staining was seen throughout the lateral. The Berlin 41-25H awaits completion
operations to maximize its production potential.
Respectfully submitted,
Ross Huls
Sunburst Consulting, Inc.
November 4, 2014

off white, pink, soft, amorphous to earthy texture

RE:
HORIZONTAL WELL
BERLIN 41-25H
NENE Section 25-151N-93W
MOUNTRAIL County
Well File # 29172
Dear Natalie:
Pursuant to Commission Order No. 24255, approval to drill the above captioned well is hereby given. The approval is granted on
the condition that all portions of the well bore not isolated by cement, be no closer than the 200' setback from the north & south
boundaries and 500' setback from the east & west boundaries within the 1280 acre spacing unit consisting of Sections 25 & 36 T151N
R93W. Tool error is not required pursuant to order.
PERMIT STIPULATIONS: Effective June 1, 2014, a covered leak-proof container (with placard) for filter sock disposal must be
maintained on the well site beginning when the well is spud, and must remain on-site during clean-out, completion, and flow-
back whenever filtration operations are conducted. MARATHON OIL COMPANY must take into consideration NDAC 43-02-
03-28 (Safety Regulation) when contemplating simultaneous operations on the above captioned location. Pursuant to NDAC
43-02-03-28 (Safety Regulation) "No boiler, portable electric lighting generator, or treater shall be placed nearer than 150 feet to
any producing well or oil tank." All distances on the Production Layout Plat must comply with NDAC 43-02-03-28 (SAFETY
REGULATION). This well is located on an aquifer: An onsite inspection is required. Contact NDIC Field Inspector for site
specific stipulations to include but not limited to: Closed Mud System, no drilling pit, and impermeable liner is required on the
entire location and a string of casing must be placed in the rat and mouse hole and cemented to ground level. Furthermore, the
operator must take into consideration the production facility when placing the liner on location. Due to drainage adjacent to
the well site, a dike is required surrounding the entire location. MARATHON OIL CO must contact NDIC Field Inspector
Robert Garbe at 701-720-3262 prior to location construction.
Drilling pit
NDAC 43-02-03-19.4 states that "a pit may be utilized to bury drill cuttings and solids generated during well drilling and completion
operations, providing the pit can be constructed, used and reclaimed in a manner that will prevent pollution of the land surface and
freshwaters. Reserve and circulation of mud system through earthen pits are prohibited. All pits shall be inspected by an authorized
representative of the director prior to lining and use. Drill cuttings and solids must be stabilized in a manner approved by the director
prior to placement in a cuttings pit."
Form 1 Changes & Hard Lines
Any changes, shortening of casing point or lengthening at Total Depth must have prior approval by the NDIC. The proposed directional
plan is at a legal location. Based on the azimuth of the proposed lateral the maximum legal coordinate from the well head is: 10081'S and
645'E.
Location Construction Commencement (Three Day Waiting Period)
Operators shall not commence operations on a drill site until the 3rd business day following publication of the approved drilling permit
on the NDIC - OGD Daily Activity Report. If circumstances require operations to commence before the 3rd business day following
publication on the Daily Activity Report, the waiting period may be waived by the Director. Application for a waiver must be by sworn
affidavit providing the information necessary to evaluate the extenuating circumstances, the factors of NDAC 43-02-03-16.2 (1), (a)-(f), and
any other information that would allow the Director to conclude that in the event another owner seeks revocation of the drilling permit,
the applicant should retain the permit.
Permit Fee & Notification
Payment was received in the amount of $100 via credit card. It is requested that notification be given immediately upon the
spudding of the well. This information should be relayed to the Oil & Gas Division, Bismarck, via telephone. The following information
must be included: Well name, legal location, permit number, drilling contractor, company representative, date and time of spudding.
Office hours are 8:00 a.m. to 12:00 p.m. and 1:00 p.m. to 5:00 p.m. Central Time. Our telephone number is (701) 328-8020, leave a
message if after hours or on the weekend.
Natalie Menge
August 19, 2014
Page 2
Survey Requirements for Horizontal, Horizontal Re-entry, and Directional Wells
NDAC Section 43-02-03-25 (Deviation Tests and Directional Surveys) states in part (that) the survey contractor shall file a certified
copy of all surveys with the director free of charge within thirty days of completion. Surveys must be submitted as one electronic copy, or
in a form approved by the director. However, the director may require the directional survey to be filed immediately after completion if the
survey is needed to conduct the operation of the director's office in a timely manner. Certified surveys must be submitted via email in one
adobe document, with a certification cover page to certsurvey@nd.gov.
Survey points shall be of such frequency to accurately determine the entire location of the well bore.
Specifically, the Horizontal and Directional well survey frequency is 100 feet in the vertical, 30 feet in the curve (or when sliding) and 90
feet in the lateral.
Confidential status
Your request for confidential status of all information furnished to the Director, or his representatives, is hereby granted. Such
information, except production runs, shall remain confidential for six months commencing on the date the well is spud.
Confidential status notwithstanding, the Director and his representatives shall have access to all well records wherever located.
Your company personnel, or any person performing work for your company shall permit the Director and his representatives to come
upon any lease, property, well, or drilling rig operated or controlled by them, complying with all safety rules, and to inspect the records and
operation of such wells and to have access at all times to any and all records of wells. The Commission's field personnel periodically inspect
producing and drilling wells. Any information regarding such wells shall be made available to them at any time upon request. The
information so obtained by the field personnel shall be maintained in strict confidence and shall be available only to the Commission and
its staff.
Surface casing cement
Tail cement utilized on surface casing must have a minimum compressive strength of 500 psi within 12 hours, and tail cement
utilized on production casing must have a minimum compressive strength of 500 psi before drilling the plug or initiating tests.
Logs
NDAC Section 43-02-03-31 requires the running of (1) a suite of open hole logs from which formation tops and porosity zones
can be determined, (2) a Gamma Ray Log run from total depth to ground level elevation of the well bore, and (3) a log from which the
presence and quality of cement can be determined (Standard CBL or Ultrasonic cement evaluation log) in every well in which production
or intermediate casing has been set, this log must be run prior to completing the well. All logs run must be submitted free of charge, as
one digital TIFF (tagged image file format) copy and one digital LAS (log ASCII) formatted copy. Digital logs may be submitted on a
standard CD, DVD, or attached to an email sent to digitallogs@nd.gov Thank you for your cooperation.
Sincerely,
Alice Webber
Engineering Tech

methods and equipment are not utilized. Consult the applicable field order for exceptions.

April 9, 2014
RE: Filter Socks and Other Filter Media
Leakproof Container Required
Oil and Gas Wells
Dear Operator,
North Dakota Administrative Code Section 43-02-03-19.2 states in part that all waste material associated with
exploration or production of oil and gas must be properly disposed of in an authorized facility in accord with all
applicable local, state, and federal laws and regulations.
Filtration systems are commonly used during oil and gas operations in North Dakota. The Commission is very
concerned about the proper disposal of used filters (including filter socks) used by the oil and gas industry.
Effective June 1, 2014, a container must be maintained on each well drilled in North Dakota beginning when the
well is spud and must remain on-site during clean-out, completion, and flow-back whenever filtration operations
are conducted. The on-site container must be used to store filters until they can be properly disposed of in an
authorized facility. Such containers must be:
leakproof to prevent any fluids from escaping the container
covered to prevent precipitation from entering the container
placard to indicate only filters are to be placed in the container
If the operator will not utilize a filtration system, a waiver to the container requirement will be considered, but
only upon the operator submitting a Sundry Notice (Form 4) justifying their request.
As previously stated in our March 13, 2014 letter, North Dakota Administrative Code Section 33-20-02.1-01
states in part that every person who transports solid waste (which includes oil and gas exploration and production
wastes) is required to have a valid permit issued by the North Dakota Department of Health, Division of Waste
Management. Please contact the Division of Waste Management at (701) 328-5166 with any questions on the
solid waste program. Note oil and gas exploration and production wastes include produced water, drilling mud,
invert mud, tank bottom sediment, pipe scale, filters, and fly ash.
Thank you for your cooperation.
Sincerely,
Bruce E. Hicks
Assistant Director
Marathon Oil Company

General Comments:

1.
BOP EQUIPMENT
Marathon Oil Company's minimum specifications for pressure
control equipment are as follows:
Ram Type:
13 5/8" 5000 psi blind, pipe and annular.
a. Due to Marathon's experience it is felt that the above
referenced BOP equipment is adequate for drilling this well.
The reduced permeability of the target zone along with
Marathon's area experience of drilling over 150 horizontal
wells indicate that a MASP of 3000 psi is more adjusted to
the reality of the reservoir.
BOP and other equipment testing:
a. Floor valve, dart valve, kill valves, check valve, manual
choke line valve, manual top drive valve, hydraulic top
drive valve, HCR, choke house valves, choke manifold,
choke hose, choke line, kill line, upper pipe rams, lower
pipe rams, blind rams (Low Test: 250 psi x 5 min. High
Test: 5000 psi x 10 min.)
b. Annular Preventer (Low Test: 250 psi x 5 min. High Test:
2500 psi x 10 min.)
c. Rotating head and Orbit Valve (Low Test: 250 psi x 5 min.
High Test: 1500 psi x 10 min.)
Frequency:
a. After initial installation (NU BOPE).
b. Whenever any seal subject to test pressure is broken.
c. After any repairs compromising seal.
d. At 30-day intervals.

ABNORMAL PRESSURES AND H2S GAS
a. The maximum anticipated bottom-hole pressure is 7810 psi.

6.
Well Completion
a. A 4 ½" liner will be run from above the 7" casing shoe to
the bottom of the well.
Liner has frac sleeves
installed.
b. Tie back liner will be run from top of 4 ½" Liner back to
the surface.
c. Well will be fractured utilizing a 30 stage frac.
d. Pursuant to NDIC letter effective February 12,2014,
concerning Hydraulic Fracture Stimulation using Diesel
Fuels, Marathon Oil Company will not inject diesel fuel
or any diesel-type chemicals (68334-30-5, 68476-34-6,
68476-30-2, 68476-31-3, or 8008-20-6) during the
hydraulic fracture stimulation process or this well.
Marathon understands the guidelines that are outline in
the above referenced letter including the requirement to
obtain an Underground Injection Control, Class II permit
from the NDIC prior to commencing any Hydraulic Fracture
Stimulation in which any amount of diesel fuel or any
diesel type chemical is injected.

RE:
Application for Permit to Drill (APD)
Berlin 41-25H
NENE Sec 25-151-93
Dear Todd,
Please find attached the documents that accompany the APD for the above captioned wel . This
application was submitted using the e-filing process on-line. Please process the APD and use the
Credit Card Marathon has on file with your office for the processing fee.
This well will be drilled off an expansion to the original Brodahl 31-25H (NDIC# 18153) wel pad.
There will not be a cuttings pit for this well. Cuttings will be transported to Clean Harbors for
disposal.
As per the address request issue, we have contacted Corey Bristol, Mountrail County Chief
Deputy Emergency Manager , to request a legal street address for these wells per the
requirements in NDAC 43-02-03-16.
Please keep all information confidential
If you have any questions or require more information, please contact Natalie Menge, Bill Groffy
or Joe Schneider Regulatory Compliance Representatives at 701-456-7500
wfgroffy@marathonoil.com or JJSchneider@Marathonoil.com , nmenge@marathonoil.com
Thank You.

Gas Capture Plan
Brodahl Pad
Sec 25 T151N R93W
Field: Re-Union Bay
Flowback Strategy
Anticipated First Production date
First production date from the new wells is currently scheduled for February 2015. There is an existing gas
connection on this location.
Multi-well startup
The well is expected to flowback concurrently with one of the other wells on the location. Flowback of each well is
expected to be approximately 4-10 days in duration.
Anticipated Oil and Gas Rates
Average Gas Rate from the wellpad during flowback is anticipated to be around 3,100 MSCFD
Average Oil Rate from the wellpad during flowback is anticipated to be around 3,800 bopd

Alternatives to flaring
Use of gas on lease, including fuel gas for Heater Treaters, is an alternative to flaring that is intended for this
location as well as connection to a gas pipeline.
Other alternatives to flaring are noted in NDIC order 24665.
